  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_518061ce-8407-4152-b667-fcd84900164b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText12636421576459434509" style="display:none">The extraordinary new adult fantasy of magic in our world and the price we pay for it by the author of THE SPIDERWICK CHRONICLES.	<br />	<br />Cassel is cursed. Cursed by the memory of the fourteen year old girl he murdered. Life at school is a constant trial. Life at home even worse. No-one at home is ever going to forget that Cassel is a killer. No-one at home is ever going to forget that he isn't a magic worker.<br /><br />Cassel's family are one of the big five crime families in America. Ever since magic was prohibited in 1929 magic workers have been driven underground and into crime. And while people still need their touch, their curses, their magical killings, their transformations, times have been hard. His granddad has been driven to drink, his mother is in prison and his brothers detest him as the only one of their family who can't do magic.<br /><br />But there is a secret at the centre of Cassel's family and he's about to inherit it. It's terrfying and that's the truth.<br /><br />The White Cat is a stunning novel of a world changed by magic. In this world only 1% of the population can work magic but they have the power of nightmares.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yup. But the book will explain later (aka. around the middle to near end) why and how the first couple chapters happen. In other words: imagine the bo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yup. But the book will explain later (aka. around the middle to near end) why and how the first couple chapters happen. In other words: imagine the book is like a numbers line from 0 to 10. You don't start at 0, you start at 2 or 3 instead.<br /><br />PS: i'm bad with words :P Hope this helps.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/72114572-mary"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/72114572-mary">Mary</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No one can tell the workers and nonworkers apart so if a worker decided to take off their glove, no one would know if they are a worker and about to w<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No one can tell the workers and nonworkers apart so if a worker decided to take off their glove, no one would know if they are a worker and about to work someone else. This way there’s less discrimination between workers and nonworkers and extra protection from workers. Also they only wear gloves because a worker is only supposed to be able to work with their hands<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_613374694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613374694" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/613374694?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575096714" href="/book/show/7804123-white-cat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2014">best-of-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=thriller-crime">thriller-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer613374694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12392152247712401352"><b>[read 2 | May 2020]</b><br/>Rereading this made me <i>so happy</i> I don't even know how to properly explain the satisfied warmth covering my whole soul right now. It had been six years! SIX years!! I freaking love Holly Black; I love her style that's both simple but worked with raw depth, with characters who leap off the page in just a few lines, and protagonists you honestly would die for despite them being <i>pretty as the devil and twice as clever</i>. Honestly love that. Keep it up Cassel, sweetie, you're doing y</span>
  <span id="freeText12392152247712401352" style="display:none"><b>[read 2 | May 2020]</b><br />Rereading this made me <i>so happy</i> I don't even know how to properly explain the satisfied warmth covering my whole soul right now. It had been six years! SIX years!! I freaking love Holly Black; I love her style that's both simple but worked with raw depth, with characters who leap off the page in just a few lines, and protagonists you honestly would die for despite them being <i>pretty as the devil and twice as clever</i>. Honestly love that. Keep it up Cassel, sweetie, you're doing your best.<br /><br />Teen con artists. Crime families. Morally grey plotlines. Twisty finales and tricky mind games. Fractious brotherly relationships. Magic but also highschool and homework. It's just all so deliciously, wickedly good. I wish this one could make a comeback after the hype of The Cruel Prince.<br /><br /><br /><i>(this old review is cringely flaily but I leave it there because baby!Fury really loved freaking out. 😂) </i><br /><br /><b>[read 1 | November 2014]</b><br /><b>This is literally the best and most underrated book ever!</b> I feel like my new life goal is going to be shouting about this book from the rooftops. IT IS THAT GOOD. It's mind-numbingly good. It has some of the best plot twists and character development. It's basically Supernatural meets the mafia.<br /><br /><b>Crime...ohhh I love crime books.</b>It's like a family business, being a worker. You get born a curseworker though, so Cassel, who is the youngest of a worker family is a non-worker and that's...kind of hard for him. His big brothers are deep into the family work for crime bosses. They work for Zackeroff. Cons. Crimes. Murder. Blood money.<br /><br /><b>Cassel is one of my favourite characters of all time now.</b> He's a con man (although to be honest, he sucks at lying) and he's got a smart-mouth and he's absolutely awesome. He's 99% flawed. But he loves his family. No matter how screwed up his family is. Which is a lot considering his mother's in jail, his brothers work for a crime lord, and his dad is dead.<br /><br />I love books about family and warped families. With Cassel's brothers so criminal and his mother in jail and yet Cassel <i>still</i> put them first. Also Cassel spends a lot of time with his Grandfather, who's a death-worker. I loved that too. The grandpa cared and loved Cassel, but didn't absolutely smother him. I LOVE THE ENDING THOUGH. Family means so so much...but what do you do when your family does things you can't forgive?<br /><br /><b>There are actually a few friends too.</b> Not a lot, because Cassel doesn't do friends (he has a Big Bad Secret hanging over his life). But I loved Sam and Danika. They were perfection, just in the story enough to make it pop with brilliance but yet not having to be Cassel's #1 concern. <br /><br /><b>CAN WE JUST TALK ABOUT THE INSANELY GOOD PLOT TWISTS?!!</b> I so would die happy if I ever wrote even a quarter as well as this. This is insanely awesome. Everything was perfectly explained and Holly Black brought us into this world with no excessive info-dumping and no utter confusion. I love it I love it I love it.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- oh my GOSH. I cannot believe how much I grinned when I realised Cassel was the transformationist. I knew it'd be someone unexpected, but I thought it was one of his brothers. CASSEL, THOUGH?!! Best. twist. ever. I just couldn't get over how his brothers basically used Cassel as their murder weapon. He thinks he's the kid who's stuffed under the floorboards and no one cares about him because he's "Not a worker" but in reality he's their #1 asset. <br />- That chair Cassel hates on? Well, I reckon it's a person or something. I actually wonder if their entire grubby cluttered house is partially filled with objects that used to be human. Don't you reckon??<br />- And now I totally don't think Cassel's dad died in a car accident. Did Cassel kill him?? Omg. I need book 2. <br />- Lila is an AMAZING character. She is just...woah. She is a bully and she's exceptionally well written. I hate her and love her at the same time. <br />- I have no idea where book 2 is going. But I'm going to love it.<br />- And I love Cassel so much because he's brothers are downright sociopaths and cruel and insane and yet HE STILL SAVES THEM.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It goes on my shelf of Favourites. Perfection, pure perfection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12392152247712401352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_170456037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170456037" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170456037?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416963974" href="/book/show/8731014-white-cat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=readalong">readalong</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170456037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17184017031732755748"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>Holly Black, where have you been my whole life? <br/><br/><b>We are, largely, who we remember ourselves to be. That’s why habits are so hard to break. If we know ourselves to be liars, we expect not to tell the truth. If we think of ourselves as honest, we try harder.</b><br/><br/>But what happens when you are forced to doubt every single memory that makes you who you are?!<br/><br/>This book has definitely made it to my ‘top ten young adult books’ list. It came at the right time and it was just what I needed: angst-free a</span>
  <span id="freeText17184017031732755748" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br />Holly Black, where have you been my whole life? <br /><br /><b>We are, largely, who we remember ourselves to be. That’s why habits are so hard to break. If we know ourselves to be liars, we expect not to tell the truth. If we think of ourselves as honest, we try harder.</b><br /><br />But what happens when you are forced to doubt every single memory that makes you who you are?!<br /><br />This book has definitely made it to my ‘top ten young adult books’ list. It came at the right time and it was just what I needed: angst-free and fun. <br /><br />Let’s start with the main character, Cassel (whom I keep calling Vincent for obvious reasons). I love it when female authors succeed in creating a strong male voice, a thing that doesn’t happen often enough. Lish McBride did it in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8041873.Hold_Me_Closer__Necromancer" title="Hold Me Closer, Necromancer by Lish McBride" rel="nofollow noopener">Hold Me Closer, Necromancer</a>. Holly Black did it with Cassel. I really felt like I was inside a boy’s head. That’s not to say that Cassel didn’t have emotional moments and uncertainties, of course he did, they were just handled differently. In creating this character, Black followed all the usual conventions, but in a way that was new and refreshing. For example, <i>I just want to be normal</i> is a very common problem for YA protagonists and I usually find it eyeroll-inducing. With Cassel it felt genuine, probably because he didn’t whine about it, but instead acted in such a way that made him look more like other people his age. The desire was present in all his decisions – from the school he chose to attended to the girl he used to date. <br /><br />Cassel comes from a family of curse workers, people with magical ability (only they call it talent, not magic) to influence other people using minimal skin-to-skin contact. His mother is an Emotion worker currently in jail for working some very rich guy into falling in love with her, his grandfather can literally kill people with a single touch and his two older brothers are extremely talented as well. Cassel is the only one without a real talent, a fact he makes up for by being an excellent con artist and an occasional thief – both skills that are highly admired in his family. <br /><br />White Cat kept me interested from start to finish. I could read this type of stories for the rest of my life without getting bored. It’s always interesting when your narrator can’t be sure of his own memories or anything else for that matter, but when you have all that in first person, it’s especially confusing and so much fun! <br /><br />Favorite quote:<br /><i>I consider kissing her right there on the dirty couch, but some instinct of self-preservation stops me. Once someone’s hurt you, it’s harder to relax around them, harder to think of them as safe to love. But it doesn’t stop you from wanting them. Sometimes I actually think it makes the wanting worse.</i><br /><br />The fascinating and detailed world Holly Black created left me wanting more! I can’t wait to get my hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8288246.Red_Glove__Curse_Workers___2_" title="Red Glove (Curse Workers, #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Glove</a> audio, narrated by Jesse Eisenberg. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17184017031732755748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_171576657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171576657" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171576657?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171576657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5774111510568099061"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I really, really enjoyed pretty much everything about this book. An exciting mystery, memorable characters and a touch of magic... I can't express how excited I am about reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8288246.Red_Glove__Curse_Workers__2_' title='Red Glove (Curse Workers #2) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Glove</a> as soon as possible.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black' title='Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holly Black</a> is an author that never really did anything for me before. I gave up on <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_' title='Tithe (The Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tithe</a> after reading just one chapter, and her Spiderwick Chronicles weren't bad children's books but they didn't really stand out from the masses either. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_' title='White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>White Cat</a> was completely different, I was</span>
  <span id="freeText5774111510568099061" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>I really, really enjoyed pretty much everything about this book. An exciting mystery, memorable characters and a touch of magic... I can't express how excited I am about reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8288246.Red_Glove__Curse_Workers__2_" title="Red Glove (Curse Workers #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Glove</a> as soon as possible.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> is an author that never really did anything for me before. I gave up on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_" title="Tithe (The Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a> after reading just one chapter, and her Spiderwick Chronicles weren't bad children's books but they didn't really stand out from the masses either. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_" title="White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">White Cat</a> was completely different, I was addicted from chapter one. I loved Cassel - the protagonist - and found his voice believably male but easily relatable for me at the same time. The story is laced with humour from the very first page when we are introduced to our protagonist dangling from a roof in his underwear.<br><br>Basically, Cassel comes from a family of curse-workers (those who have various gifts such as memory manipulation, dream manipulation, etc.) and struggles with the burden of being ungifted and, therefore, an outsider even in his own home. Oh, and he happened to murder his best friend three years ago. Despite this, he has managed to build up some semblance of a normal life at his boarding school; well, that is, until the dreams about the white cat start occurring. A white cat that seems to want to tell him something. And then his brothers start acting strange and it becomes more and more obvious that secrets are being kept and Cassel is being lied to.<br><br>There's all sorts going off and the story is never boring, and every time the mystery appears to be solved, something else will happen. This is one of those books with many little mysteries to solve so even the most astute reader will find it difficult not to be surprised. I thought the whole novel worked very well and I will be starting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8288246.Red_Glove__Curse_Workers__2_" title="Red Glove (Curse Workers #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Glove</a> with a keen interest in what will happen to Cassel next. I'm only giving it 4.5 stars because this series has just begun but it's definitely one of my favourite books of the year.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5774111510568099061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2177663311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177663311" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177663311?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=us-ya">us-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177663311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14748811062448387817"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560183235i/27647228._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><b>Curse workers </b>- <b>hated, feared, beloved.</b><br/><br/>Some can make you <b>forget your own name.</b> Others can kill you with a single touch. Rarest of all - some can even transform you into something entirely different.<br/><br/>But don't forget, <b>their powers are a curse. </b><br/><br/>They <b>experience a backlash </b>with every use of their powers. If a luck worker gives you good fortune, they will experience a pleasant kickback. If they give too much luck, they may spend forever in a blissed out state. <br/><br/>The <b>backlash can be unpredictable</b>: if</span>
  <span id="freeText14748811062448387817" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560183235i/27647228._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><b>Curse workers </b>- <b>hated, feared, beloved.</b><br><br>Some can make you <b>forget your own name.</b> Others can kill you with a single touch. Rarest of all - some can even transform you into something entirely different.<br><br>But don't forget, <b>their powers are a curse. </b><br><br>They <b>experience a backlash </b>with every use of their powers. If a luck worker gives you good fortune, they will experience a pleasant kickback. If they give too much luck, they may spend forever in a blissed out state. <br><br>The <b>backlash can be unpredictable</b>: if a death worker kills you, part of them will die - a tooth, or a finger, or maybe even their heart. <b>Most curse workers are tied to the black market</b> or other criminal enterprises. Cassel's family is in the thick of it. <blockquote>
  <i>Clever as the devil and twice as pretty</i>
</blockquote>Cassel comes from a long line of <b>curse workers and criminals.</b> He's the only one from his family without powers but he does his best to keep up with the family business - whether it be running an <b>illegal betting ring </b>in his high school or scamming tourists with trinkets. <blockquote>
  <i>I can't trust the people I care about not to hurt me. And I'm not sure I can trust myself not to hurt them, either.</i>
</blockquote>Oh, and <b>he killed best friend</b> Lila (daughter of a mob boss) three years ago. <b>He doesn't know how, or why, </b>or what could've triggered him to do that. He only remembers that he can't remember.<br><br> <b>Could he have really killed Lila? </b>And if not him, who?<blockquote>
  <i>We are, largely, who we remember ourselves to be. That's why habits are so hard to break. If we know ourselves to be liars, we expect not to tell the truth. If we think of ourselves as honest, we try harder.</i>
</blockquote> The only issue I had with this book was that <b>the world was more fleshed out than the characters.</b> I craved more details on the curse workers and all their power rather than the (somewhat) plodding plot. <br><br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Whoa. Jesse Eisenberg narrated this one - it felt like I was listening to a movie. Very well done narration.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14748811062448387817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1141316309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11257394059818771335"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423841565i/13680984._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>Reread 10/30</u> : Cassel is still the sarcastic little shit I remembered. I have no other option than loving him even more.</b> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"I hate that I love this. I hate that the adrenaline pumping through the roots of my body is filling me with giddy glee. I'm not a good person."</b>
</blockquote><br/>This book was full of <i>charms</i> ← <i>See what I did there?</i> <br/><br/>▧ <b><u>Charm ⁂1</u> : I do love me some liar</b> ⁂<br/><br/>Beware of Cassel Sharpe, professional liar and Master of the game of make-believe. <i>You're going to love him.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"Being a con artist means thin</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11257394059818771335" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423841565i/13680984._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>Reread 10/30</u> : Cassel is still the sarcastic little shit I remembered. I have no other option than loving him even more.</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I hate that I love this. I hate that the adrenaline pumping through the roots of my body is filling me with giddy glee. I'm not a good person."</b>
</blockquote><br>This book was full of <i>charms</i> ← <i>See what I did there?</i> <br><br>▧ <b><u>Charm ⁂1</u> : I do love me some liar</b> ⁂<br><br>Beware of Cassel Sharpe, professional liar and Master of the game of make-believe. <i>You're going to love him.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Being a con artist means thinking that you're smarter than everyone else and that you've thought of everything. That you can get away with anything. That you can con anyone.<br>I wish I could say that I don't think about the con when I deal with people, but the difference between me and my mother is that I don't con myself."</b>
</blockquote><br><b>Charming, deceptive, untrustworthy, sarcastic, selfish : Of course I loved Cassel, what do you think?</b> Since he was fourteen and well, hmm, <i>killed</i> his best friend and first love, Cassel learnt that to survive he has to become a Master of pretending. All the time. <br><br><i>Friendship?</i> Nothing more than an exchange of goods. Who'd want a killer of a friend? Yeah? No hands raised? That's what I thought. <br><br><i>Love?</i> Yeah, sure. A good way to fake normality.<br><br><i>Family?</i> You mean the <i>curse workers</i> who always kept him in the dark and fed him with snippets of affection? Them? <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I'm not good at having friends. I mean, I can make myself useful to people. I can fit in. I get invited to parties and I can sit at any table I want in the cafeteria.<br>But actually trusting someone when they have nothing to gain from me just doesn't make sense.<br>All friendships are negotiations of power.”</b>
</blockquote><br>Don't get fooled, despite the fact that he basically tries to con everyone, we can't avoid seeing the extreme vulnerability that all his tricks can't hide, and then... Then we 're dealing with a charming <i>and</i> hopeless male-lead we can't help but care about. <br> <br>▧ <b><u>Charm ⁂2</u> : Of course I'm lost! And I love it.</b> ⁂<br><br><b>What a multi-layered mystery!</b> Each time I thought I finally got it the truth slipped through my fingers. There are many subplots in this story and that's for the best : we never know who Cassel can trust, <i>damn</i>, we don't even know if we can trust Cassel most of the time! Everything can be a con and this makes every decision or action suspect - try to overtake Cassel's shenanigans and you'll see. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Marks think they can get something for nothing.<br>Marks think they can get what they don't deserve and could never deserve.<br>Marks are stupid and pathetic and sad.<br>.....<br>Marks forget that whenever something's too good to be true, that's because it's a con."</b>
</blockquote><br>As for the <b>writing</b>, I have to point that I was pleasantly surprised by Holly Black. Indeed it's my first book from this author and I must admit that I was really wary at first. What a fool I've been! It was <b>a captivating page-turner</b> that never bored me. <br><br>▧ <b><u>Charm ⁂3</u> : Why can't I be a curse worker, huh? Why?</b> ⁂<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423841719i/13681020._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Never <i>ever</i> forget your gloves, otherwise you are likely to experience one of these <i>delightful</i> experiences :</b><br>✔ To find yourself somewhere without any idea how you came<br>✔ Be changed in a cockroach. Yeah, that sucks.<br>✔ To start sobbing in remorse for something you didn't even do.<br>✔♪♫♬ Beware of the music you hear. ♪♫♬ <i>Just sayin'</i><br><br>▧ <b><u>Charm ⁂4</u> : Applaud the cat. Just do it. He's got <i>claws</i>.</b> ⁂ <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399544028ra/9565191.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

      Emily May
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=to-read-in-2020">to-read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231984846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17957354130594453650">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/white-cat-by-holly-black.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>Well, well, well. Color me surprised. Just when I decided <i>never</i> to read another <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black' title='Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holly Black</a> work again (due to our seemingly conflicting ideas about what good writing is), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171576657' rel='nofollow noopener'>Emily's review</a> of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_' title='White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>White Cat</a> convinced me to give the author one final try. And, who knew, I really, really liked it. Actually, this book is one of the strongest YA UF novels I've ever read. I am not exactly sure what made Black change her writing style so drastically, but I won't be complaining. Some</span>
  <span id="freeText17957354130594453650" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/white-cat-by-holly-black.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />Well, well, well. Color me surprised. Just when I decided <i>never</i> to read another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> work again (due to our seemingly conflicting ideas about what good writing is), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171576657" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily's review</a> of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_" title="White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">White Cat</a> convinced me to give the author one final try. And, who knew, I really, really liked it. Actually, this book is one of the strongest YA UF novels I've ever read. I am not exactly sure what made Black change her writing style so drastically, but I won't be complaining. Somehow her characters are no longer repulsive and her writing is a lot more polished than before. <br /><br />As for the story itself, I thought it was fantastic. It is set in an AU America where certain people have magic abilities (they are called "curse workers"). They can manipulate emotions, change memories, bring luck or death. The magic is "worked" through touch. Cassel, the narrator, belongs to a family of curse workers/con artists. He can do cons too, but has no magic abilities. When he finds himself sleepwalking on the roof of his school dorm, haunted by the memories of a dream where a white cat asks for his help, Cassel embarks on a trip to discover mysteries of his past, present and the white cat.<br /><br />Even though I'd read way too many reviews of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_" title="White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">White Cat</a> before starting the novel, I still managed to be thoroughly mystified by its plot. I attribute it to the fact that this book has a bit of <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0209144/" rel="nofollow noopener">Memento</a>-esque quality to it, with gradual unraveling of the mysteries tangled up by various cons and curse works. (Or my usual denseness wherever any kind of mystery-solving is involved.)<br /><br />And can I say <i>Yay for mafia and con artistry?</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6087756.White_Cat__Curse_Workers___1_" title="White Cat (Curse Workers, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">White Cat</a> gave me what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9858517.All_These_Things_I_ve_Done__Birthright___1_" title="All These Things I've Done (Birthright, #1) by Gabrielle Zevin" rel="nofollow noopener">All These Things I've Done</a> couldn't - just enough crime, backstabbing and cons to keep me glued to its pages/my iPod. <br /><br />Can't wait to get my hands on the sequels. Cassel's mom is up to no good. And what will he do about Lila?<br /><br />I guess the lesson here is <i>Never say never</i>?</span>

<div id="review_2449398926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2449398926" />
    <a title="Laura Herondale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52844833-laura-herondale"><img alt="Laura Herondale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550655303p2/52844833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2449398926?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Herondale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Herondale" href="/user/show/52844833-laura-herondale">Laura Herondale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Laura by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=own-e-book">own-e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449398926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4972351347688615138">4.5*<br/><br/><b>*Spoiler free review*</b><br/><br/>I went into this book expecting to like it, because the premise sounded awesome, but I was wary, since it’s not exactly a book I see all around goodreads. But this blew my expectations out of the park. I loved this book, like, a lot. To the point where I can’t even form coherent sentences to explain <i>why</i> I loved this book so much. But I can’t read the next book in this trilogy until after I finish my review, so here I am trying (and probably failing) to string together a </span>
  <span id="freeText4972351347688615138" style="display:none">4.5*<br /><br /><b>*Spoiler free review*</b><br /><br />I went into this book expecting to like it, because the premise sounded awesome, but I was wary, since it’s not exactly a book I see all around goodreads. But this blew my expectations out of the park. I loved this book, like, a lot. To the point where I can’t even form coherent sentences to explain <i>why</i> I loved this book so much. But I can’t read the next book in this trilogy until after I finish my review, so here I am trying (and probably failing) to string together a few thoughts that actually make sense.<br /><br />So, I’ll start with the <b>plot</b>: This book follows <b>Cassel</b>, the only member of his family who doesn’t possess magical powers (known as curseworkers). Doing magic (or working) was banned, and so most curseworkers and curseworker families become criminals. Cassel has grown up in a family of conmen, and has learned to become one himself, despite his lack of magic. He’s put up a whole facade of normalcy around his life; he goes to a normal school with normal kids and acts as normal as he can pretend to be. But Cassel’s not like these kids, he never can be, because he’s got a secret: he killed his Best Friend three years ago. But just when Cassel’s beginning to fit into his new life at boarding school, an incident of sleepwalking unravels his carefully crafted facade, and he begins to realise that there’s something going on that he doesn’t know about. His family is keeping secrets, and Cassel begins to suspect that they’re conning him. So, he needs to find out what’s being hidden from him, so he can con them back.<br /><br />Honestly, that description doesn’t do this story justice, though. It’s such an interesting plot, full of secrets and lies, all wrapped up in a whole load of family drama. It’s like a mob story, but with magic. There was never a point during the book when I wasn’t intrigued by what would happen next; when I could physically stop turning pages. And everything just came together so well; all of these pieces were being fit together, and by the end, everything made sense. <br /><br />Speaking of the end, whilst everything was wrapped up satisfyingly, Holly Black threw a bloody curveball and now there’s more drama that Cassel needs to work through in the second book, and I have no idea how he’s going fix any of what happened.<br /><br />I did, however, have many ideas about the plot of this book. And by ideas, I mean predictions. Correct predictions. Because as much as I loved this book, I found everything very predictable. I pretty much knew what was going on before I’d even gotten through the first third of the book. This didn’t ruin the story, or even greatly affect it, but I do have to mention this, because this would’ve been a five-star read for me if it weren’t for this.<br /><br />Anyway, now that I’ve gotten my one negative point about this book out of the way, I’m free to rave about it!<br /><br />So, <b>characters</b>: I’m not going to say much about Cassel’s family, because that’ll just lead me right into spoiler territory, and I want to keep this review spoiler free in the hopes that I can convince a few people who haven’t read this book yet to give it a try. What I will say, though, is this: I hated all of them except for his grandfather. And I don’t mean to say that they were badly written characters or anything like that, because they weren’t that <i>at all</i>. I thought they were all extremely intriguing, and each had their own dimensions that made them very interesting to read about. I loved them as characters. But I <b>HATED</b> them as people. They were just so bad at being brothers. I have 3 younger brothers, and I couldn’t imagine ever treating them the way that Cassel’s Brothers treat him. The worst part is that I liked Barron at first. I mean, Phillip was always a dick, but I thought Barron was sweet. And then he started doing some stuff I didn’t like, and eventually I hated him as much as Phillip. And his mum! She meant well, I think (I hope), but it felt like she was just continuously screwing up, and I just don’t know how she hasn’t learned by now?? At least his grandpa was great; he was hilarious, cared for Cassel, and was still bad ass. I want more of him in the next one, because he was instantly someone I loved the first time he was mentioned, and I continued to love him for the rest of the book.<br /><br />And then there was the female protagonist; I really enjoyed reading about her. She didn’t play a huge role in the story until the end, but based on the final chapter, I’m pretty sure she’s going to be a big part of the next book. But I thought she was an incredibly interesting character, and I wanted to know more about her. She was kind of a bitch, but she was also really smart and determined. And she was really self-aware; like, she knew she was a bully, but she accepted that, and used it to her advantage in certain situations. And it was so sweet to see how much she did for the people she cared about. She put herself in danger to save her Father, and protected Cassel despite her conflicted feelings about him.<br /><br />But, she isn’t who I really want to be talking about rn. Neither is Cassel’s family. It is Cassel, himself, that I want to talk about because dAMN I LOVE HIM. Like, I would read about this kid (I say kid, we’re the same age, lol) doing laundry. And to show you all how much I love him, I figured I’d show you the first few notes I took on him (all from the first chapters, so no spoilers dw):<br /><br /><i>“It’s impossible to have problems with a girlfriend who’s no longer mine.”</i><br /><br />Me: Lol, I love this guy<br /><br /><i>“‘Nothing! Just that I was sleepwalking, not trying to kill myself. And if I wanted to kill myself, I wouldn’t throw myself off a roof. And if I was going to throw myself off a roof, I would put on some pants before I did it.’”</i><br /><br />Me: Yep. Definitely love him.<br /><br /><i>“Her name was Lila, she was my best friend, and I loved her. I killed her anyway.”</i><br /><br />Me: Oh shit, I’m intrigued. Is he a psychopath? Why did he do it?<br /><br /><i>“I don’t think about what music I like; I think about what music I should like.”</i><br /><br />Me: Wow. He’s so intriguing. Like he seems like a psychopath, but he loved Lila, so he can’t be? Damn, ok. I’m in. Holly Black, I am yours.<br /><br />And these are just my notes from chapter one. I have an entire paragraph about how much I love Cassel later on in my notebook (side note: ughhhhh discovered whilst reading this book how much I HATE not being able to take notes in the book. This is why I don’t use the library as much as I should). I should probably explain why I love him though. Because right now I sound like a babbling mess.<br /><br />Ok, so, reason number 1 that I loved Cassel: I could relate to him so much. Like he’s constantly feeling like an outsider, even with people who should be comfortable around. He lies to everyone to cover up the fact that he’s different. And he has major trust issues. Like:<br /><br /><i>“I can’t trust the people I care about not to hurt me. And I’m not sure I can trust myself not to hurt them, either.<br /><br />Friendships suck.”</i><br /><br />I wrote this quote down, underlined it twenty times, wrote “I relate to this boy on a spiritual level” and then underlined that twenty times. Every though Cassel has was a thought I have had at some point in my life. And I loved that. Here’s another one (yes I am just going to quote the whole book because it was amazing and you all need to read it):<br /><br /><i>“But actually trusting someone when they have nothing to gain from me just doesn’t make sense.”</i><br /><br />Like, Cassel is me, I am Cassel. Just his cynicism towards the world is everything I am, and it was so nice to see that in someone else.<br /><br />I also just loved him because of how sweet and adorable he is. Like, he loves his family so much, even though his brothers are dicks and his mum screws his life up over and over again. Even when he finds out something horrible about his brothers, he still wants to protect them. He’s such a cinnamon roll, and I want to protect him with everything I am. Especially since he’s kind of dumb. Like, the blurb of this book will have you believe he’s smart and ruthless, but he’s actually naive and adorable. Like, he’s skeptical about everyone except his family, but they’re the only conmen he knows. He’s kind of blinded by his love for them, and whilst I thought that was really sweet, it meant that a lot of the time, he believed in them, even when he shouldn’t have. <br /><br />But, he was very good at conning people. It was so interesting to see how his brain worked when coming up with a con. And Holly Black didn’t try to do that thing that some authors do where they make it so their characters aren’t doing anything bad because they like it. Like, Cassel full on loved conning people, and that was really refreshing to see. It feels like nowadays in books, you get all these characters that are unlikeable because the author tries too hard to make them likeable, and they end up being a big contradiction. But Cassel conned people, not only because he had to sometimes and because he grew up conning people and so that’s the way he knows to live, but also because he LIKED it. And I loved reading about that. It made his character really interesting to read about, and so I loved him even more. But like, also, I really just loved him because hE’S LEGIT ME. One more (I’m sorry):<br /><br /><i>“I don’t know how to explain how afraid I am of being judged.”</i><br /><br />I LOVE HIM.<br /><br />Ok, so at this point I know you all think I’m a wreck (and I am), but I’m hoping you’re still reading this, because this next part is the main reason I loved this book (aside from Cassel, obviously). <b>The world building</b>: I’m absolutely in love with this world. Well, it’s urban fantasy, so the world is technically ours. But Holly Black has woven curseworkers and their magic into our world and it’s history, to the point where it’s almost a completely new world. Everyone wears gloves, because curseworkers work people with their hands. The government is considering passing a new law that states that everyone must be tested to see if they’re a worker, and there are protesters worried about all the consequences that’ll come of that. Australia was founded by curseworker prisoners, and as a result, a far higher percentage of Australian’s are curseworkers. There are songs and tv shows about and/or featuring curseworkers. And slang that people use to talk about curseworking. The whole magic system is so deeply ingrained into the culture of our world that it’s practically a different world. And because of this, it was so immersive. I felt like I was living there, in this alternate version of New York, hanging out with Cassel. <br /><br />And it was easy to immerse myself in this world because of how well Black integrated the world building into the story; there was never a point where it felt like I was reading a bunch of info dumps. Certain aspects of the world were introduced when I needed to know them, and I really appreciated this. It felt like the actual plot never had to stop or pause just so that the world could be explained more, so the story felt more fluid and was easier to read. <br /><br />I also just thought the magic system was so Creative and different to anything I’ve seen before. Like yeah, I’ve seen magic systems that have the same premise: characters can use their hands to control something, whether it be an element, the weather, or, in this case, people. But the way Holly Black has done it is very unique. there are 7 types of curseworkers: luck, emotion, body, death, transformation, dreams, and memory. Some are more common than others, but all are quite rare in the general population. They can control a person’s luck, emotions etc depending on what type of worker they are, but (and here’s the interesting part), they’ll suffer from ‘blowback’ for doing so. The blowback is more or less extreme, depending on what they’ve done to someone. And it can be positive or negative, depending on what they’ve done to someone. So if a luck worker gives someone a little bit of good luck, they’ll be a little more lucky. If they give someone a lot of bad luck, they’ll be extremely unlucky, too. I LOVE this aspect of the magic system; it makes it so no one feels invincible, because there’s always consequences for a curseworker when they work someone. It creates an extra layer of depth to the world and it’s politics; curseworking is banned, but not all curseworkers are evil. They don’t all want to be, because that would harm them as well. But by banning them, it puts them in a situation where the only thing they CAN be is criminals. It just makes everything about the world so much more interesting.<br /><br />Ok, so the last thing I’m going to talk about is the <b>romance</b>, and there’s not much to talk about, so dw, this essay of a review will be over soon. Pretty much all I want to say is that I really appreciate how the romance didn’t AT ALL take over the plot of the story. I’m so sick of books where characters are in life-or-death situations and all they can think about is that hot girl they just met or whatever. But that doesn’t happen in this book. The romance is very subtle and builds up throughout the course of the book, through flashbacks and present day events. And by the end, you’re rooting for them. But it’s a very small subplot. I’m pretty sure it’s going to be a bigger part of the second book, but this first book took the time to get me invested in the romance, so I’m actually excited about that (though I’m also really worried about it for reasons you wouldn’t understand unless you read the book). <br /><br />But yes, my point is that I love this book. Like, a lot. And you should all go read it :)<br /><br />Pre-review: My emotions are all over the place. I'm kind of a mess. So I'm going to take a moment to work out my thoughts, and then I'll write up my review (which will probably still be incoherent). At this point, all I can say is thank you to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27036454-helena-fc" rel="nofollow noopener">Helena</a> for simultaneously completing and destroying my life :))))) (&lt;-- me smiling through the pain rn, because damn I'm a wreck)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4972351347688615138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13045628366399729582">At first when I read the blurb I saw mobsters and con artists and was like, I don't know man, that doesn't sound good. I've loved everything else so far by Holly Black, so I was like, well, let me go ahead and take a chance on this. Plus, what a weirdly cool title. And I LOVE weird things!<br/><br/>Cassel was so awesome, and it felt nice to read a whole book from a guy's perspective. Also, he seemed like a real teen boy. And the magic system? Very interesting with the whole we-have-to-wear-gloves-thing. I</span>
  <span id="freeText13045628366399729582" style="display:none">At first when I read the blurb I saw mobsters and con artists and was like, I don't know man, that doesn't sound good. I've loved everything else so far by Holly Black, so I was like, well, let me go ahead and take a chance on this. Plus, what a weirdly cool title. And I LOVE weird things!<br /><br />Cassel was so awesome, and it felt nice to read a whole book from a guy's perspective. Also, he seemed like a real teen boy. And the magic system? Very interesting with the whole we-have-to-wear-gloves-thing. It's one of the best urban fantasies I've read!<br /><br />There are some pretty great twists, and that freaking ending! Oh man, I need to start the next book. Seriously!</span>

<div id="review_458332980" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458332980" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458332980?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575096714" href="/book/show/7804123-white-cat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=contains-annoying-characters">contains-annoying-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=dragging">dragging</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458332980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15326923017403325283"><b>Final rating: 2/5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398008i/768684._SX540_.png' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “The thing is that it’s really hard to stop discrimination when something’s illegal,” the girl says. “I mean, everybody thinks of workers as being criminals. Like, people use the word ‘worker’ to mean<br/>criminals. And, well, if we work a work, even once, we are criminals. So most of us are, because we had to figure it out somehow and that was usually by making something happen.”<br/>“And there are lots of workers who never do anything bad. They go to weddings and hospital</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15326923017403325283" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 2/5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398008i/768684._SX540_.png" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “The thing is that it’s really hard to stop discrimination when something’s illegal,” the girl says. “I mean, everybody thinks of workers as being criminals. Like, people use the word ‘worker’ to mean<br>criminals. And, well, if we work a work, even once, we are criminals. So most of us are, because we had to figure it out somehow and that was usually by making something happen.”<br>“And there are lots of workers who never do anything bad. They go to weddings and hospitals and give people good luck. Or there’s people who work at shelters and they give people hope and make them feel confident and positive. And that word—‘cursing.’ Like all we can do is bad magic. I mean, why would you even want to do the bad stuff? The blowback’s awful. Like, if all a luck worker ever does is make people have good luck, then all he has is good luck too. It doesn’t have to be bad.”<br>“Magic,” the girl says. “It’s just all magic.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I don't get whats up with the hype about this book? It definitely sounded promising but...there are lot of buts around. This is a story about a guy[Cassel] who killed his best friend [Lila], and the white cat who is stalking him. Sounds weird but ok......(right?)?<br><br>Anyways, the paragraph above explained the status of so called "workers", and i was wondering why the author didn't put it in the beginning in the first place. It just made the story pointlessly confusing at times. Not to mention that lack of fast revealings got the story quite slow, and add to it loooooooong chapters and there you have it. I thought about dropping it in the middle, but i decided to stick till the end (because i can't just drop it before i read it all, not my style xD). So, the last 1/4 was extremely entertaining - actually really awesome &gt;:D, while 3/4 of the book were confusing and quite boring. Which is why i am gave this 2 stars. <br><br>Not to mention, first 3/4 of the book were <b> absolutely predictable </b>. I could already connect that:<br>1. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cat was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Lila  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, <br>2. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cassel was a worker with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ transformation powers (which is the ultimate awesome power. And that he didn't <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ kill Lila, but turned her into cat.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>,<br>3. the brothers were actually hiding the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cassel was actually one of them.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br>I <b> didn't </b> predict though that the brothers Philip and Barron (MAJOR SPOILER) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ used Cassel to kill people, then erased his memory and that they were doing it from the accident with Lila  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br>___________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>CHARACTERS</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>___________________________________________<br><br>Not to mention, i didn't like any of the <b> characters. </b><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Cassel</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br><b>Cassel</b> is totally boring guy. I usually love when books are told from first person view but only when it is the guy who is the narrator, but Cassel, Cassel just irritated the hell out of me. I don't think i succeeded in having sympathy for him at all. He is the type of the teenage girls in whose story everybody is keeping secrets and she doesn't know anything about it. Oh, and everyone here <i> are </i> keeping secrets from Cassel, under the "you are not worker so we can't tell you anything". <br>So.......he is the non-worker in worker family. <i>Check</i>. He doesn't have powers. <i>Check</i>. Boring. <i>Check</i>. Irritating. <i>Check</i>. Not to mention: average. <i>Check</i>.<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>The white cat:</u>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>i can't really say anything about it, except it is an object of horrors. Hahahhaha. <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Lila:</u>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>Meet <b>Lila:</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386106528i/7292943._SY540_.png" width="500" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ironically, i was watching anime "K", where there is a girl called Neko, which has strikingly same appearance as Lila from the flashbacks (except for the length of her hair). Cute.<br>And that is all i am going to say about her. Except, i don't like her so much.<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Everyone else:</u>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>All of them were annoying me. Except Cassel's mother. She didn't have time to annoy because the whole book she was in Jail. Barron and Philip - i wanted to slaughter them. But as they say, everything for the family. <br>___________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>___________________________________________<br><br> Characters were very much annoying, and the plot was cofusing and boring at times, but it does have strong ending. Therefore, only the ending was enough for me to not drop this series. I just hope that the second book will be better than White Cat. I really hope so. <br>____________________________________________<br><br>&gt;&gt;&gt; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458332984" rel="nofollow noopener">My review for Red Glove (Curse Workers, #2)</a> &lt;&lt;&lt; <br><br><br><b>
  <i>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i>
</b><br><a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/2013/05/white-cat-curse-workers-1-by-holly-black.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363317i/714576.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12384556878650222887">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Your average 2010 YA but with some modern perks. Holly Black was ahead of the game even back then 🤧<br/><br/><b>This book was surprisingly dark and twisty.</b> I really enjoyed following Cassel around in his search for clues. I didn’t find the world building mindblowing, but it was fun to read about some kind of parallel reality in which everyone wears gloves to protect themselves and others from magic.<br/><br/><b>My main issue with this book is that for a good 60% not a lot happens.</b> I was almost halfway through an</span>
  <span id="freeText12384556878650222887" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Your average 2010 YA but with some modern perks. Holly Black was ahead of the game even back then 🤧<br /><br /><b>This book was surprisingly dark and twisty.</b> I really enjoyed following Cassel around in his search for clues. I didn’t find the world building mindblowing, but it was fun to read about some kind of parallel reality in which everyone wears gloves to protect themselves and others from magic.<br /><br /><b>My main issue with this book is that for a good 60% not a lot happens.</b> I was almost halfway through and I was considering dnfing it, but I’m glad I didn’t. What made me keep going was Cassel. He’s a lovely main character, and if I had read this around five or six years ago, I would have had a crush on him lol! The cool thing is that he’s funny and sometimes very naive, but he also just cons people like that and he doesn’t care a single bit. <b>Man, I love his duality.</b><br /><br /><b>This was a fun mystery and honestly, compared to other YA books published in those years, it stands out.</b> The plot isn’t a given right away, and the book definitely uses tropes, but not blatantly. For example, there is something that resembles a love triangle but it’s not the usual one because it’s layered. The chosen one narrative is there too, but the main character relies on his cleverness instead. <br /><br /><b>So, I quite enjoyed this book, but I don’t think I’m ever going to read book 2.</b> I should’ve read this when it first came out, I’m sure it would have been one of my favorite series.</span>
