<div id="review_635295955" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635295955" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/635295955?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/12969590-maythavee">Maythavee</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=serious-cliffhanger">serious-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635295955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10021663614492400576"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Lie until even you believe it-that's the real secret of lying. The only way to have absolutely no tells.<br/>Too bad I'm not quite there yet.</i>
</b><br/><br/>When I try to think of a word that reminds me of this book, the most forthcoming is just this: <b>Weird. This book was all kinds of weird.</b> But, when I take the time to really delve deeper and actually peel back the layers of this intricate story-line, I begin to 'see' so many more words pop into my mind: <b>Haunting, clever, mesmerizing, addicting...swe</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10021663614492400576" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Lie until even you believe it-that's the real secret of lying. The only way to have absolutely no tells.<br>Too bad I'm not quite there yet.</i>
</b><br><br>When I try to think of a word that reminds me of this book, the most forthcoming is just this: <b>Weird. This book was all kinds of weird.</b> But, when I take the time to really delve deeper and actually peel back the layers of this intricate story-line, I begin to 'see' so many more words pop into my mind: <b>Haunting, clever, mesmerizing, addicting...sweet.</b> There are so many ways to look at a story and if you filter all the mystery out of the words, then it does, in fact, come off as a super weird book. But when you totally immerse yourself and ask 'Why is this happening?', 'What triggered this?', 'Where the <i>hell</i> is this going?', I swear that you'll find yourself racing through the pages and before you know it, you'll be closing the book. It's <b>that</b> kind of story. <br><br><b>I don't want to be a monster, but maybe it's too late to be anything else.</b><br><br>Cassel is one of those characters that really gets under your skin. You don't quite know why you like him, but you find yourself laughing at his sarcasm, feeling pain for this kid who grew up feeling like the most insignificant member of his family. You find yourself smiling at his charm and your heart breaking when he thinks of Lila, his childhood best friend (and only friend), and the girl he killed years ago. This sounds shady as fuck, I'll give you that, but in this world, everyone wears gloves to hide their 'curse' and to prevent their touch from doing irreparable damage by making contact with someone's skin. This is a world where children grow up around con workers as mothers and fathers and sisters and brothers. Even if you aren't involved with the con work, there's still a chance you've been 'cursed' and are considered a worker. This simply means you might have a touch that causes selective memory loss, luck, death, etc. But with each of these 'gifts' there is ample cost-<b>No gift in their world comes without a price.</b><br><br><b>I hate that I love this. I hate that the adrenaline pumping through the roots of my body is filling me with giddy glee. I'm not a good person.</b><br><br>You're probably still wondering about how he murdered his best friend and the girl he's always been in love with, right? I didn't know how I'd feel about it, personally. But, for whatever reason, I found myself identifying with him, sympathizing for him, hoping it was all a misunderstanding and that he had been worked. See, Cassel is the only one in his family without a gift-he is the only non-curse worker. I think this made him a really sweet and relatable character, and all the more identifiable as someone who had significantly screwed up in his past. And, more than that, it was devastating to see how much he just wanted his brothers to love him and accept him, but instead they grew up stomping him under their foot as if he was an insignificant piece of trash, just because they could. Now, I can't say nothin' about anythin' but I will say this-If you grew up with a deplorable family that did deplorable things...what keeps them from conning you?<br><br><b>Marks think they can get something for nothing.<br>Marks think they can get what they don't deserve and could never deserve.<br>Marks are stupid and pathetic and sad.<br>.....<br>Marks forget that whenever something's too good to be true, that's because it's a con.</b><br><br>At times I found this to be very dark and even somewhat disturbing, but that was more at the beginning. Once I began to see everything unwind, it all started to make sense and I became fully immersed in figuring out what was wrong with the distorted picture we were being given. Lies upon lies, and betrayals on top of betrayals, we don't get a clear picture until the end-and even then it's like looking through fractured glass. It was excellent.<br><br><b>The easiest lies to tell are the ones you want to be true.</b><br><br>Altogether an amazing story that I couldn't put down even for a minute. More than once I was covering my mouth with my hand to stifle a gasp and begging for a better end than what was coming for Cassel. In a way, this book was almost told through an unreliable source's eyes and we are left wondering what's reality and what's make-believe. I loved this aspect. Each time we learned something, we realized there was so much more to the story and it never really stopped growing as a plot, it never really and truly ended. So, I absolutely cannot wait to start book two. If it's even half as good as this one I will be ecstatic...but more than that, I can't wait to see what becomes of Cassel and his new-found 'friends.' He's still trying to figure all that out. And that cliffhanger-agh!!!<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>

<div id="review_204639993" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204639993" />
    <a title="Janina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3455554-janina"><img alt="Janina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404584313p2/3455554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204639993?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janina" href="/user/show/3455554-janina">Janina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416963974" href="/book/show/8731014-white-cat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=cats">cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=mystery-thriller-suspense">mystery-thriller-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204639993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7844318006503199390">Okay. This book has the word “cat“ in its title. How could I ever hesitate to read it?<br/><br/>Simply put, I was rather less enamoured of Holly Black's Modern Faerie Tales series and actually couldn't see myself picking up another one of her books. I had given her two chances, and she hadn't convinced me. Don't get me wrong, Tithe and Ironside certainly weren't bad, but I'm normally looking for something better than not bad. Positive reviews abound made me look closer into White Cat, though. And I didn't</span>
  <span id="freeText7844318006503199390" style="display:none">Okay. This book has the word “cat“ in its title. How could I ever hesitate to read it?<br /><br />Simply put, I was rather less enamoured of Holly Black's Modern Faerie Tales series and actually couldn't see myself picking up another one of her books. I had given her two chances, and she hadn't convinced me. Don't get me wrong, Tithe and Ironside certainly weren't bad, but I'm normally looking for something better than not bad. Positive reviews abound made me look closer into White Cat, though. And I didn't regret it. <br /><br />Cassel comes from a family of curse workers, magicians wielding their power by touch. Curse work is illegal, so basically, Cassel also comes from a family of criminals. His mom can work emotions (and doesn't hesitate to use this talent to her advantage), his grandfather death – only Cassel can't work anything. Yet, there is something mysterious going on with him. He keeps dreaming of a white cat and a girl he once knew but tried to erase from his memory. He sleepwalks. He can feel that there is something wrong, but nobody will talk to him about it …<br /><br />This story is fresh and new. It is set in a world that is so similar to ours, yet strikingly different in certain aspects and features a main character that is broken, feels left out, clearly shows criminal talent, but never crosses the border into unlikable. There are clans of curse workers dominating the underground – reminiscent of the mafia – and a family that definitely deserves to be called problematic: A mother in jail, two brothers associated the most feared worker in the whole country and more than one skeleton in the closet. And on top of all that, there is a very special cat.<br /><br />I loved this book's atmosphere. In parts, it had something of an old black-and-white movie, quiet and mysterious – gentlemen with leather gloves pulling out guns, secret meetings in dark places. Yet, it was also firmly rooted in the modern world. Cassel's friends from school added a certain light-heartedness to the story and Cassel's subtle humour in general really suited me. I just immensely liked his character and felt extremely close to him despite our many differences. <br />Additionally, Black never felt the need to explain her world to me. It was just there the way it was, and she left it to me to figure things out. I love to be introduced to a new setting that way and hate nothing more than detailed explanations as to why certain things are the way they are. It makes me feel like I'm not taken seriously as a reader. <br /><br />All in all, a series I look forward to continuing. This book was full of surprises and unforeseeable twists, shady villains and sometimes even shadier allies. It is definitely one of those stories where you can't trust anybody to tell you the truth (not even the narrator), but I for my part really enjoyed the suspense this created.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7844318006503199390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307711816" href="/book/show/7067782-white-cat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer210359477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13596420877115751331">It's safe to say that it's not the cover that attracted me to this book. I was actually quite surprised to see its many great reviews. Yes, I'm a book judger. Oh well. I picked this up as an audiobook and actually liked it a lot.<br/><br/>Some people are born as workers in Cassel's world. Workers can "work" people with their hands. By touching someone, they can alter their memory, kill, give good luck, bad luck. You name it. Cassel is the only one in his family who is not a worker. He's been getting these</span>
  <span id="freeText13596420877115751331" style="display:none">It's safe to say that it's not the cover that attracted me to this book. I was actually quite surprised to see its many great reviews. Yes, I'm a book judger. Oh well. I picked this up as an audiobook and actually liked it a lot.<br /><br />Some people are born as workers in Cassel's world. Workers can "work" people with their hands. By touching someone, they can alter their memory, kill, give good luck, bad luck. You name it. Cassel is the only one in his family who is not a worker. He's been getting these weird dreams that make him sleepwalk in very unfortunate scenarios.<br /><br />I found the plot of this book very original and quite fun. I loved Cassel, the protagonist. I loved that it was a male lead. They're so rare but they're great. No girly angst. Cassel was charismatic and I quite enjoyed the narrative by Jesse Eisenberg. His voice was very fitting for Cassel's character. The plot twists aren't too difficult to figure out. But it didn't hinder my enjoyment of the story. It was still fun to walk through it with Cassel and see him figure it out. <br /><br />The book isn't dark. But i think it may be heading that way. Cassel is very innocent in the start, so I think it contributed to the lighter, fun read. By the end, though, we saw glimpses of grimier times with conspiracies and intricate politics. <br /><br />I'm happy that I gave this one a chance regardless of the dreadful cover. It's not what I expected at all. I was also told the sequel is just as good. This is one to not pass up if you like paranormal.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_164140802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164140802" />
    <a title="Ceilidh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh"><img alt="Ceilidh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422140120p2/3229028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164140802?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceilidh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceilidh" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh">Ceilidh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164140802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11274733001738195200">Holly Black is the anti-Cassandra Clare. While Black’s series has been using cover quotes from Ms Clare (a good friend of Ms Black) to promote the series, Black’s writing stands leaps and bounds beyond anything Clare has ever written and “White Cat” is a brilliant read on pretty much every level. <br/><br/>It’s not often these days that I’m surprised by a YA book. Maybe it’s the market itself, maybe it’s my own YA oversaturation, but whatever the case may be, when a YA comes along that I find entertaining</span>
  <span id="freeText11274733001738195200" style="display:none">Holly Black is the anti-Cassandra Clare. While Black’s series has been using cover quotes from Ms Clare (a good friend of Ms Black) to promote the series, Black’s writing stands leaps and bounds beyond anything Clare has ever written and “White Cat” is a brilliant read on pretty much every level. <br /><br />It’s not often these days that I’m surprised by a YA book. Maybe it’s the market itself, maybe it’s my own YA oversaturation, but whatever the case may be, when a YA comes along that I find entertaining, creative, exciting, witty and mysterious and makes it all seem so effortless, I can’t help but get excited. (The book is classified as YA by some and adult sci-fi/fantasy by others, but since it was in the YA section of my library, I’ll classify is as such.) <br /><br />Even if crime based novels aren’t your thing, I highly recommend this book. Taking the concept of underground crime families and adding magic to the equation, Black has created an exciting, detailed world full of depth and intrigue, populated by a wide variety of interesting characters and genuine surprises. There’s a definite Sopranos-style vibe throughout the novel, as double crossing and black market jargon are casually discussed, but it fits in wonderfully with a well crafted and extremely readable mystery. How refreshing to see this sort of story in YA where the stakes are genuinely high and things are at true risk. The pacing is quick and smooth, even during quieter moments where Black skilfully manages to avoid turning discussions into info-dump sessions. The way the crime world is intertwined with the magic element is almost seamless and I was particularly fascinated by the different types of magic workers and how their gifts are also curses. Black’s writing style is very much suited to this type of story; it’s crisp, often sparse, very witty and avoids any sort of unnecessary visits into the town of purple prose. <br /><br />The narrator of this tale, Cassel Sharp, is a joy. That sounds like an exaggeration but hear me out. One, he actually sounds like a man. Two, he manages to be tortured and scared without ever becoming whiny or overwrought, which is no easy feat. His familial interactions are interesting and never quite what they seem (The Sharps themselves are a colourful bunch, all with their own secrets and problems with so much at stake.) Three, he actually grows and develops as a character! He’s a witty, sneaky and extremely intelligent man but he’s also confused, scared and haunted by his past. His family are hiding things from him, he’s hung up on his ex-girlfriend, he’s desperately trying to con his way back into school and then there’s those dreams that plague him. Everything is handled with skill and wit. He’s definitely one of the best protagonists in YA right now. It’s also incredibly refreshing to see the small romantic element of the story not completely overwhelm the plot. It’s something that’s definitely on Cassel’s mind but he’s got other things to worry about and he knows how to prioritise! Outside of Cassel, I had a huge soft spot for his grandfather as well as his mother. She’s only featured a few times and only ever in phone call conversations but you can feel her presence throughout the book. She’s definitely the head of the clan and it shows. I can’t wait for more of her in the sequel.<br /><br />If I was to criticise anything about this book, it would be this small thing. The cons are described in great detail, which is fascinating, and Cassel frequently tells us, as do many other characters, how great they are at the job, but then they immediately screw up. It got a bit repetitive but luckily didn’t spoil this wonderful book for me. <br /><br />I heartily recommend “White Cat” to everyone, especially those of you who, like me, were getting a sick of paranormal YA. It’s not quite an accurate label for this series but Black excels in her field with this series, creating an intricate world with intrigue, complexities and fascinating characters, and I am thoroughly excited by the prospect of getting my hands on the sequel. <br />4.5/5.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11274733001738195200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1425989093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425989093" />
    <a title="Lia  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48295288-lia"><img alt="Lia  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594824825p2/48295288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1425989093?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia  " href="/user/show/48295288-lia">Lia  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=english-and-american-lit-and-more">english-and-american-lit-and-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=magic-and-supernatural-things">magic-and-supernatural-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=amazing-characters-are-amazing">amazing-characters-are-amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=main-character-is-on-point">main-character-is-on-point</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=fictional-boyfriend">fictional-boyfriend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425989093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9609401876784693743">I expected to like this book the same way you like to watch baking shows or cat videos on Youtube. That said, I didn't expect to love it as much as I did. <br/><br/>White Cat was absolutely mind-blowing. 5 stars was the only possible way I could rate it because honestly?, I have nothing to complain about (which I know, is so unlike me, but here we are). It took me literally five hours to finish the book, because it was completely impossible for me to put it down. Everything about it was exactly as I wante</span>
  <span id="freeText9609401876784693743" style="display:none">I expected to like this book the same way you like to watch baking shows or cat videos on Youtube. That said, I didn't expect to love it as much as I did. <br /><br />White Cat was absolutely mind-blowing. 5 stars was the only possible way I could rate it because honestly?, I have nothing to complain about (which I know, is so unlike me, but here we are). It took me literally five hours to finish the book, because it was completely impossible for me to put it down. Everything about it was exactly as I wanted it.<br /><br />I think that one of the reasons for which I connected so strongly with this book is that I could see myself in the MC, Cassel. I know that's probably not the best reason, but he usually did things as I would have, and his mind wasn't so different from mine. <br />This is a book about a charming liar: someone who can flash a smile, say the right words at the right time and fool you while you don't even understand what's happening. But Cassel is not only an excellent actor, he's also human and vulnerable, and I could feel his very own emotions as if I were the one experiencing them - his guilt, his regret, but also his fury. He isn't the kind of person that just waits for things to happen, but he was the one moving the plot forward, and I liked that he was smart, but not unbelievably so. He was very intuitive, but there were still times when he had no idea what was going on, and I liked that. <br /><br />The writing was very good. It wasn't particularly flowery, but I enjoyed it nonetheless, and I think this series has the potential to be a new favorite of mine. I like mysteries and I like magic, and the book was slightly creepy at times, which is always a plus. Also, I'm well known to have a weakness for books that explore family dynamics, especially when they're about difficult sibling relationships.<br />And, well, this book has organized crime in it. I know what you're thinking: <i>so what?</i> But, guys. Martin Scorsese is my favorite director. I know every line of Goodfellas by heart, and I think The Departed is a masterpiece. So yeah, crime families are <i>definitely</i> my kind of thing.<br /><br />I'm going to stop right here, because this review is honestly just me fangirling like crazy over this wonderful book. But I honestly can't wait to get my hands on the second one!<br />White Cat is one of the best books I've read this year, probably one of the best books I've read period. I read it on my Kindle because I'm lazy and didn't have a lot of money to spend, but I think I'm going to get the physical copy of it as well, so that I can place it on my shelf and sigh contentedly whenever I pass by it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9609401876784693743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_907627693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907627693" />
    <a title="jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21073355-jade"><img alt="jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381337827p2/21073355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907627693?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jade" href="/user/show/21073355-jade">jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21073355-jade?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907627693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer833937689097820783">I had low expectation about this book because urban fantasy could be hard for me to get into. Besides, it’s not encouraging that the book is in a male voice by a female author. Therefore, I had only intended to take a look at the first page. However, first page turned into second page and so forth. I couldn’t put it down. All the while I was reading, I kept trying to stop and switch to the book I had in mind. Well, I never did. And here I am, eager to finish the whole series.<br/><br/>It's surprising how </span>
  <span id="freeText833937689097820783" style="display:none">I had low expectation about this book because urban fantasy could be hard for me to get into. Besides, it’s not encouraging that the book is in a male voice by a female author. Therefore, I had only intended to take a look at the first page. However, first page turned into second page and so forth. I couldn’t put it down. All the while I was reading, I kept trying to stop and switch to the book I had in mind. Well, I never did. And here I am, eager to finish the whole series.<br /><br />It's surprising how real and likable the male voice, Cassel, is. You'd never mistake him as a girl. Cassel is a con artist with a conscience. At 17, he has a terrible past and has gone through quite some hardship. He struggles to find his place but never wallows in self-pity. Instead, he meets the challenges head on without getting overly sentimental. There's a sense of humor even in a really bad situation. He has that vulnerability and self-depreciation to make you root for him, and to see him out-smart powerful adversaries is such a satisfying feeling. <br /><br />The book has the obvious <i>Sopranos</i> vibe going on but it's mostly within YA range. And the mystery! It's fascinating to connect the dots. Clues are dropped here and there, while the world-building is effortlessly weaved into the story. There's never long passages of info dumping, which is quite impressive given how detailed and creative this magical world is. <br /><br />Though this book may not be a heady emotional ride that tugs at your heartstrings, it is nonetheless a cleverly written, engrossing story with rich world-building and likable characters. I'll definitely continue with the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="833937689097820783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3024031737">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_167042068" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167042068" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167042068?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307711816" href="/book/show/7067782-white-cat">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167042068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14101460358946348425">I don’t have a quote because by the time he said something I liked I got myself into a faff trying to get my notebook and then find my pen and then it wouldn't work and… it was just too much hassle. <br/>Oh and also, I don’t really know how Ms Black is spelling all her character names so apologies if they’re wrong. <br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>Curses + Mob Families + Secret Underground World = Um, YES. The whole idea behind this series is absolutely <i>genius</i> and the world that Black creates is just spectacular. I reall</span>
  <span id="freeText14101460358946348425" style="display:none">I don’t have a quote because by the time he said something I liked I got myself into a faff trying to get my notebook and then find my pen and then it wouldn't work and… it was just too much hassle. <br />Oh and also, I don’t really know how Ms Black is spelling all her character names so apologies if they’re wrong. <br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br />Curses + Mob Families + Secret Underground World = Um, YES. The whole idea behind this series is absolutely <i>genius</i> and the world that Black creates is just spectacular. I really want to move so I can have an excuse to buy <a href="http://www.corneliajames.com/gloves/showitem.asp?1194,0,0,1,7" rel="nofollow noopener">these</a> gloves Heebie Jeebies. Cassel. Fraternal love. Asian housemates. Kitty Cats. A love story I could get behind. Grandpas. Sleepwalking. Blood packs. Jailbird Mums. <br /><br /><b>Low Point.</b><br />OK Cassel, you are amazingly cute (and I know you’re supposed to be of Indian heritage but I kept picturing you as <a href="http://imstars.aufeminin.com/stars/fan/luke-pasqualino/luke-pasqualino-20090307-497591.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> lovely chap. Mmmmhmm.) and you’ve been through a lot. But gosh you are <u>dim</u>. But more on this in your own section, boyo. <br />I also would have liked this book to be a bit darker. There is a lot of really grim stuff hinted at (What <i>did</i> Cassel actually do?/ Grandpa channelling his inner Dumbledore/ Blowback) but it was never really explored. Considering this book is about powerful horrifying mobsters who can destroy/control/manipulate you with their hands… this book was a far far too tame. MORE VIOLENCE PLEASE.<br />I have faith and hope that these few quibbles will be ironed out in the other books of the series. I got the impression that Ms Black was testing the waters a little bit and hopefully she’ll take the plunge and wallow in the grimy potential that these books have. <br />Also… when Mr Eisenberg was chatting on about the cats in Cassel’s back garden all I could think of was <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h6CcxJQq1x8" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a>. So I would giggle to myself nervously... because what <i>would</i> happen if cats had thumbs?<br /><br /><b>Hero.</b><br />Right, back to Cassel. I really did like Cassel. He was funny and smart and, like I mentioned before, I’d definitely fancy him in real life… even if he did randomly change race for no reason. <br />But by gum was he dumb. Seriously, it took him forever to realise what was happening around him and <i>I know, I know</i>… the story does kind of explain why he was all confused but… Mate, you’re supposed to be a conman, you’re supposed to be on the ball. <br />When it got to the big reveal scenes and Cassel was all like ‘What?! WHEN DID THAT HAPPEN?!’ I got really confused because I thought we’d already found that out. I’m obviously too clever for my own good.. but yeah, Cassel. Sort it out. <br />Also, please become more gruff and angry. You’re on your way but I would like more ‘Oomph’ next time. I’m awarding you a ‘B’ at the moment but you need to pull your socks up.<br />Also, you are very forgiving. This would be commendable in most circumstances but I’m sure no one would judge you if you threw a punch at a wall or ate the last piece of pizza or something equally as aggressive. Get your own back!<br />All these points will make no sense whatsoever if you haven’t read this book but I needed to get them off my chest. <br />I did like Cassel though and I thought Ms Black/Mr E did a great job in portraying your bumblingness and your honesty… even if you are a little slow. It’s endearing…. Ish. <br /><br /><b>Best Friend.</b><br />I loved Sam and Danika (Daneka? Danecka? Whatevs), Cassel’s friends from school. Sam is a complete goof who, even though he was also a little thick and didn't react normally in situations where it would be OK to freak out, I would like to be friends with him. And get drunk with him… because I can imagine him being a great drinking buddy. And buying the first round. <br />And D (gonna stick with that) was also great if not a little bit of a cliché goody two-shoes. But I think these two will get to stretch their legs a little in the next two books… or at least I hope so. <br /><br /><b>Love Interest.</b><br />I don’t want to say much about this but I really loved what Black did with this. It was original and, considering the cracked out circumstances, really realistic. <br />And also…. I can’t believe I’m saying this.<br />But if we’re heading in Triangle Infested Waters…. I think I’ll be OK with it.<br />Urgh, I feel dirty.<br /><br /><b>Baddie(s).</b><br />OK, these baddies have potential. Especially two of them. <br />But I was a little disappointed with one of them…. I was expected him to get all Brando-esque. But alas, he did not. <br />Apologies for the vagueness… but spoilers are lurking.<br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TTQwmQX82Qc&amp;feature=relmfu" rel="nofollow noopener">Memory- Elaine Page.</a><br />I’M KIDDING.<br /><i>Or am I?</i><br />I was at first but then I listened to the words several times (for research purposes only, of course. And then I had to watch <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GDZ5QJOsSNs&amp;feature=relmfu" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> just to be sure my reasoning was correct… *ahem* ) and realise that the lyrics are poignant and beautiful and particularly apt for our fluffy white titular character.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <br />
  <i>Touch me/ It’s so easy to leave me/ All alone with my memory/ Of my days in the sun/ If you touch me/ You’ll understand what happiness is/ Look a new day has begun.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Um, I’m pretty sure Trevor Nunn wrote this song with this book in mind.<br />But fine… I know people hate musicals <s>because they are ridiculous human beings who have no sense of JOY in their lives and have no soul</s>.<br />So you can have this one which has no relevance whatsoever except it talks about cats and it allows you to make strange noises when you sing along to the chorus. But you made your choice…. Yeah, you made your choice. <br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mcUza_wWCfA&amp;feature=player_embedded" rel="nofollow noopener">Lovecats- The Cure.</a><br /><br /><b>Angst Level. </b><br />5/10. Like I mentioned before, there was definitely a sense of darkness looming within these pages (or in my headphones… um…) and one that could really have been really affective and harrowing if explored deeper. I have my appendages crossed for this to be remedied in the next books, which I can’t wait to read.<br />Also, for the emotional stuff… Cassel isn’t really a whinger which is great, because there was a great chance that this book could have been filled with countless ‘WHY ME?!’s. But it wasn’t. <br />Ms Black seemed to set the groundwork for a slightly more unhinged Cassel (which, considering the circumstances… is perfectly understandable.) which, again, I hope gets developed in the next books.<br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who are looking for a great new series to sink their teeth into. People who like the dark side of magic. People who like pretty, sparkly stones. People who don’t understand what is going on around them… even if it has flashing lights, loud sirens and shoots glitter in your face at sporadic moments. People who wish their brothers would take them out for pizza on a Tuesday night *glares in vague direction of my brother which is probably nowhere near to where he actually is because my geography is <i>shocking</i>* People who feel that Elaine Page sings directly to their soul when she sings 'Memory'. People who thought Godfather Part 3 would have been better with more elbow length gloves.<br /><br />You can find this review and other exciting things on my blog <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14101460358946348425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_171601744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171601744" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171601744?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307711816" href="/book/show/7067782-white-cat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171601744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15480538288970190673">3 1/2 stars<br/><br/>I don’t know why I expected this book to be bad. Maybe I’ve read enough paranormal YA’s to have overload trauma flashbacks whenever the genre comes up. But guess what? This one is actually good! Chalk this one up as another triumph for goodreads recommendations.<br/><br/>I find the fantasy world that she builds here to be very compelling and intricate, and since the main character starts out the book very much out of the loop, the details are allowed to assemble and grow slowly and organically </span>
  <span id="freeText15480538288970190673" style="display:none">3 1/2 stars<br /><br />I don’t know why I expected this book to be bad. Maybe I’ve read enough paranormal YA’s to have overload trauma flashbacks whenever the genre comes up. But guess what? This one is actually good! Chalk this one up as another triumph for goodreads recommendations.<br /><br />I find the fantasy world that she builds here to be very compelling and intricate, and since the main character starts out the book very much out of the loop, the details are allowed to assemble and grow slowly and organically with nary an infodump in sight. This is a world where “curse-workers” (ie, magic users) are living underground, with the threat of the government jailing them, or abusing their powers. Cassel is a member of a long line of curse-workers, and his two older brothers work for the Zacharov family, using their abilities to further the mafia’s illegal ends. Cassel has always been the odd man out as the only member of his family to be born without powers, but following in his mother's footsteps he has become an accomplished con man. When he starts sleep walking at his boarding school and having detailed dreams involving a white cat, memories from his past begin to surface, including a traumatic incident with a girl that he loved. <br /> <br />The main character is a bit naïve to begin with, and slow to catch on to what’s really going on. This is all very understandable, once the full scope of his history is revealed…but it didn’t stop me from wanting to shout “DUH!!” at the big reveal scene. Still, he more than makes up for his initial guileless innocence in the end. I am hoping for a more ruthless, crafty Cassel in the second book. *Crosses fingers for no guilty agonizing over misdeeds.* <br /> <br />I did also spend the large part of this book wishing that it would be darker and grittier – more like the mafia from The Departed and less like the hapless mobsters from The Goonies. I think that this can also be attributed to Cassel’s initial innocence. By the end of this thing, there’s drinking, con artistry, death, and blowback. “Blowback” has to be one of my favorite elements of this book: all curse workers suffer from the magic that they perform. So for example, Cassel’s grandfather the death worker has blackened nubs of fingers, as they slowly die every time he takes a life. And, there’s a compelling piece of info about blowback at the end of the book that I can’t wait to find out more about.<br /><br />There’s a little romance here that I actually found a bit heartrending and not sickening at all! (That's kind of big for me.) There’s even a teensy preemie of a love triangle. It’s not annoying, but I still hope that it never grows legs. I love Cassel’s nerdy cohorts from school, Sam and Daneca. I hope we see more of them.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />The Dears – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KHYpTm5YjQk" rel="nofollow noopener">I Fell Deep</a><br /> <br />I’m pretty sure that all the best indie rock bands come from Canada. I guess it’s the least they can do to make up for Justin Bieber. This song makes me think about Cassel’s relationship with his brothers, and his slow awakening and rebellion.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15480538288970190673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113149304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113149304" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1876075-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113149304?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cara by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1676497-tori">Tori</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113149304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3506611172485933111">If any of you are like me you are/were put off by the cover. It looks <i>creepy</i>, right? A guy with leather gloves holding a cat? How unappealing is that? Well after reading the book I know this cover fits the book completely, and the creepiness is probably part of the point. And the cover gives it a mafia feel, which is central to the whole order of the curse workers.<br/><br/>Anyways onto what's beyond the cover. Cassel at the moment is attending a private school, trying to forget some horrendous memories t</span>
  <span id="freeText3506611172485933111" style="display:none">If any of you are like me you are/were put off by the cover. It looks <i>creepy</i>, right? A guy with leather gloves holding a cat? How unappealing is that? Well after reading the book I know this cover fits the book completely, and the creepiness is probably part of the point. And the cover gives it a mafia feel, which is central to the whole order of the curse workers.<br /><br />Anyways onto what's beyond the cover. Cassel at the moment is attending a private school, trying to forget some horrendous memories that are haunting him. He also is trying to ignore the fact that he has no curse (or gift depending on who you are asking). He feels like an outsider wherever he goes, whether it is in his family or among his classmates. Cassel comes from a family of curse workers who can bring luck, manipulate emotions, physically hurt people, kill them, all just with a touch of a hand, hence why people in this society wear gloves. Cassel has to go back to live with his family now because of a nightly episode he had at school, and now that he's back he has a feeling things aren't what they seem; especially now that he keeps seeing a white cat...<br /><br />People who know me know that I <i>really</i> like reading about sibling relationships, and this book was no different. I like to read about good relationships, but this one shows how complicated and twisted they can become. You can feel Cassel's seeking for a closer relationship with his older brothers, but can't seem to find out how to do that when they always are hiding things from him. Out of the two brothers, Phillip and Barron, I can't help but feel like Barron is the saddest of the characters of the whole book. <br /><br />The book has a dark tone to it, which makes sense because Cassel is struggling to feel normal at all cost. Surrounding him is shady secrets and deeds and even though he doesn't want to be, he can't help feeling that he falls into the same vicious cycle. Black does a good job of describing the surroundings without the story’s pace getting bogged down. I could feel myself itching and cringing when you read Cassel's description of his house and the contrast you see in other places. The whole concept of curse workers is the strongest aspect of the book. How the community is glorified and vilified at the same time. At the center of all this is Cassel who is not your typical protagonist. He's not perfect at all really, but I get where he's coming from. Though the character of Cassel feels three-dimensional I felt like we didn't get to know all the characters, but since it is a series I'm hoping the other books will expand on that. <br /><br />Now for why I couldn't give the book five stars, and basically it came down to one character. I can't reveal who it is, but suffice to say it's a girl and she gets on my nerves. Other than that though I'm eager to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8288246.Red_Glove__Curse_Workers___2_" title="Red Glove (Curse Workers, #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Glove</a> because as per usual the book leaves you at a lurch. Oh why do authors like to torture us so?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3506611172485933111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eOyf2zkbyQvjXitU4I6D0Nxwp0J3Ib9MCcWE3doKXIQk6T/PB6ufORLcU844vLGbzYDUUL6v6VQp1TAVjKra6g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer16283378558935564287">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house </span>
  <span id="freeText16283378558935564287" style="display:none">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house with a secret library.</span>
